<p>TOPIC 6</p>
<p>11.0 CHANGE AND INFORMATION SYSTEMS MANAGEMENT</p>
<p>11.1 INTRODUCTION</p>
<p>By now you are able to manage resources within the organization. However, in the current health care system, we are experiencing a lot of changes including social, technological and educational. A lot of changes also have and continue to take place in the field of information, and the development of information technology is the focus in most organizations. All these confront managers and the organizations with many challenges. This topic covers management of both change and information systems as lecture 13: 1 and 13:2 respectively.</p>
<p>LECTURE 13</p>
<p>11.2 CHANGE MANAGEMENT</p>
<p>Change has always and will always be a part of us. During your life time you must have experienced change in one form or the other such as moving from one work station to another, acquisition of new skills or introduction of new methods of nursing care delivery. We live in a world of change.</p>
<p>Change is inevitable and nurse managers should understand and anticipate the reactions to change. How well managers meet these challenges can determine whether or not an organization will survive.</p>
<p><img src="assets/images/image-20260119-3794ed3e.jpeg" alt="img-62.jpeg"></p>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h2 level="2" id="objectives">OBJECTIVES<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#objectives" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h2></div>
<p>By the end of this lecture you should be able to:-</p>
<ol>
<li>Explain the concept of change</li>
<li>Analyze the process of managing change.</li>
<li>Identify reasons for resistance to change and how to overcome it</li>
</ol>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h2 level="2" id="11-2-1-what-is-change">11.2.1 What is Change?<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#11-2-1-what-is-change" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h2></div>
<p>Change can be defined as the process of making something different from what it was.</p>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h2 level="2" id="change-management">Change Management<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#change-management" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h2></div>
<p>Yoder â€“ Wise (2007) defines change management as the overall processes and strategies used to moderate and strategies used to moderate and manage the preparation for, impact of, responses to, and outcomes for conditions new and different than what existed previously.</p>
<p>There are two basic approaches to the management of change (Bennett, 1997).</p>
<ol>
<li>To forecast all environmental changes relevant to the organization that might occur and then forecast how the organization will be affected by them.</li>
<li>To list all the organization's major functions and follow this by an analysis of environmental factors that might affect the functions.</li>
</ol>
<p><img src="assets/images/image-20260119-d151f7fa.jpeg" alt="img-63.jpeg"></p>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h2 level="2" id="activity-identify-reasons-for-change-in-your-institution">ACTIVITY: Identify reasons for change in your institution.<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#activity-identify-reasons-for-change-in-your-institution" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h2></div>
<p>Once the organization identifies the need for change, it should assess its implications. This may require :- Definition of alterations in operational methods, staffing levels and the employee's attitudes and perspectives necessary to implement alterations; new equipment and systems; Redesigning of jobs; restructuring of jobs or the organization.</p>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h2 level="2" id="11-2-2-resistance-to-change">11.2.2 Resistance to Change<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#11-2-2-resistance-to-change" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h2></div>
<p>The employees fear change because of its potential for disruption of existing status in the organization. Some of the reasons why people resist change include:</p>
<p>Page 89 of 114</p>
<p>This document is available on</p>
<p>studocu</p>
<p>Downloaded by Patrick Ngobiro (<a href="mailto:pngobiro@gmail.com" target="_blank" rel="noopener noreferrer">pngobiro@gmail.com</a>)</p>
<ol>
<li>Insecurity, fear of unforeseen consequences and threats to individual status and financial rewards that it creates</li>
<li>Skills and experience acquired may have no further value and retraining may be necessary to cope with new methods</li>
<li>Possible breaking up of work groups and interpersonal relationships.</li>
</ol>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h2 level="2" id="11-2-3-overcoming-resistance-to-change">11.2.3 Overcoming Resistance to Change<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#11-2-3-overcoming-resistance-to-change" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h2></div>
<p>To reduce or avoid resistance to change, we can help the employees to go through a change process. Kurt Lewin suggested three steps to overcome resistance:</p>
<p>i. <strong>Unfreezing</strong>: Getting rid of existing practices and ideas that stand in the way of change. This requires a high level of communication with employees to convince them that change is necessary.
ii. <strong>Changing</strong>: Teaching employees to think and perform differently.
iii. <strong>Refreezing</strong>: Establishing new norms and standard practices.</p>
<p>To implement the above process the following approaches will be necessary:</p>
<ul>
<li>
<p><strong>Education and Communication</strong>
This is to make employees fully aware of all aspects of the situation and convince them that change is essential.</p>
</li>
<li>
<p><strong>Participation and Involvement</strong>
The employees should actively participate and get involved from the beginning so as to stimulate commitment.</p>
</li>
<li>
<p><strong>Patience and Tolerance</strong>
Give support and assistance needed.</p>
</li>
</ul>
<p>A nurse manager has an important role in initiating and managing change. He/she should recognize the obstacles and assist the employees to go through the change process.</p>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h2 level="2" id="11-2-4-change-agents">11.2.4 Change Agents<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#11-2-4-change-agents" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h2></div>
<p>The role of change agents has been advocated by some managers. A change agent is a person who fosters change within an organization. More often than</p>
<p>Downloaded by Patrick Ngobiro (<a href="mailto:pngobiro@gmail.com" target="_blank" rel="noopener noreferrer">pngobiro@gmail.com</a>)</p>
<p>not, the change agent is an external management consultant who specializes in this type of work. However, Institutions can identify one of their own as a change agent. Outsiders might be more objective though they may lack the detailed knowledge of the day to day operations of the organization that the latter may have.</p>
<p>The change agent may advise on job and organization design, need for retraining and management development.</p>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h2 level="2" id="11-3-management-of-health-information-systems">11.3 MANAGEMENT OF HEALTH INFORMATION SYSTEMS<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#11-3-management-of-health-information-systems" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h2></div>
<p>Most of our health institutions have massive information about the clients/patients who are the consumers of their services.</p>
<p>They also have information on administrative matters related to staff, equipment, supplies, etc. All this information is kept in records which are either in written documents, tapes or computers. Records are an important tool in controlling and assessing the work and therefore should be accurate, accessible and useful.</p>
<p>An effective health information system is important in order to get health information required for appropriate planning and decision making. It also assists in monitoring and evaluating the various activities within the organization.</p>
<p>In this lecture, we will briefly discuss Information Technology (IT) and management of health information systems</p>
<p><img src="assets/images/image-20260119-36968d9d.jpeg" alt="img-64.jpeg"></p>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h2 level="2" id="objectives">OBJECTIVES<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#objectives" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h2></div>
<p>By the end of this lecture you should be able to:-</p>
<ol>
<li>Explain information technology</li>
<li>Describe health information systems</li>
<li>Discuss the role of the nurse in health information systems.</li>
</ol>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h2 level="2" id="11-3-1-information-technology-it">11.3.1 Information Technology (IT)<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#11-3-1-information-technology-it" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h2></div>
<p>This is the acquisition, processing and dissemination of information using computers. Whereas in the past and even today in some institutions, information handling involved dependence on paper, the emphasis now is shifting to creation, storage and transmission of information through tiny electrical impulses.</p>
<p>Page 91 of 114</p>
<p>This document is available on</p>
<p>5 studocu</p>
<p>Downloaded by Patrick Ngobiro (<a href="mailto:pngobiro@gmail.com" target="_blank" rel="noopener noreferrer">pngobiro@gmail.com</a>)</p>
<p>Paper no doubt will continue to be important as tangible product of interchange of information. Nevertheless the computers are likely to dominate the scene.</p>
<p>The advantages of use of IT include:</p>
<ul>
<li>Linking the organization to its clients and suppliers.</li>
<li>Improving operational efficiency.</li>
<li>Improving quality management</li>
<li>Enabling the organization to respond quickly to environment change.</li>
<li>Facilitating the monitoring of key performance indicators.</li>
<li>Improving management control.</li>
<li>Facilitating fast and effective decision making.</li>
</ul>
<p><img src="assets/images/image-20260119-eb2be111.jpeg" alt="img-65.jpeg"></p>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h2 level="2" id="activity-list-5-problems-associated-with-computerized-systems">ACTIVITY: List 5 problems associated with computerized systems.<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#activity-list-5-problems-associated-with-computerized-systems" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h2></div>
<p>The strategies for managing information technology Systems should incorporate all the organizational resources with particular emphasis on the following (Bennet, 1997).</p>
<ul>
<li>Staff â€“ selecting those who are best equipped to handle IT-based management systems and then training them.</li>
<li>Modifications â€“ Determining the extent of modifications to existing working methods, administrative arrangements to obtain maximum benefits.</li>
<li>Altering organizational structures to make the best use of latest IT.</li>
<li>Integrating IT into all aspects of the organization's operations.</li>
</ul>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h2 level="2" id="11-4-health-information-systems">11.4 HEALTH INFORMATION SYSTEMS<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#11-4-health-information-systems" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h2></div>
<p>This is an integrated system used in health care settings to manage patient information. It is primarily a centralized patient record of demographics, health and financial information. (Yoderwise, 2007).</p>
<p>The information is entered, stored, retrieved, displayed and communicated. A major function is to communicate and integrate patient care data and information and provide management support.</p>
<p>Health data are entered into the system from computer stations located in the various departments in the organization and stored in a central computer to be accessed by all patient care services. The systems contain a central data base that is written to and accessed by all departments; Nursing, Laboratory, Pharmacy, Radiology, Physiotherapy and so on. The programs that link the individual departments must be able to "talk" to one another in order to exchange patient data. For example the wards need access to Laboratory results or Pharmacy may need access to ward to access information like height, weight and allergy information entered by nursing.</p>
<p>Downloaded by Patrick Ngobiro (<a href="mailto:pngobiro@gmail.com" target="_blank" rel="noopener noreferrer">pngobiro@gmail.com</a>)</p>
<p>9</p>
<p>ACTIVITY: What is the role of the nurse manager in Health information systems management in your organization?</p>
<p>The nurse managers and staff must understand the patient care process from a data information knowledge perspective. They must be aware of the data collected, reasons why it is collected and decisions made based on the data.</p>
<p>The type of information tracked in this system includes:</p>
<ul>
<li>Appointments, admissions, discharges and transfers.</li>
<li>Medication profiles - prescriptions, allergy reports</li>
<li>Care planning.</li>
<li>Patient acuities.</li>
<li>Human resource eg. pay roll, staff performance, incident reports and staff scheduling.</li>
<li>Plans eg. budgeting information.</li>
</ul>
<p>The information system must provide the following (Yoder-Wise, 2007):</p>
<ul>
<li>Information confidentiality and security.</li>
<li>Uniform data definitions.</li>
<li>Standard format for transmitting data.</li>
<li>Sharing of information between departments.</li>
<li>Linking of clinical and financial information.</li>
<li>Patient specific data.</li>
</ul>
<p>An effective health information system is important in order to get health information required for appropriate planning and decision making. It also assists in monitoring and evaluating the various activities within the organization.</p>
<p><img src="assets/images/image-20260119-7bd96c2e.jpeg" alt="img-66.jpeg"></p>
<p>SUMMARY</p>
<p>This lecture covered management of change and health information systems</p>
<p>Although change is inevitable, the main reasons why people resist are insecurity and fear of unforeseen. The three steps to overcome these include unfreezing, changing and refreezing. The importance of health information systems cannot be overemphasized. The system is used in health settings to manage patient information in a centralized manner. It involves use of computers where data is entered, stored, retrieved, displayed and communicated.</p>

<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h2 level="2" id="12-0-quality-management-in-nursing-care-services">12.0 QUALITY MANAGEMENT IN NURSING CARE SERVICES<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#12-0-quality-management-in-nursing-care-services" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h2></div>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h3 level="3" id="12-1-introduction">12.1 INTRODUCTION<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#12-1-introduction" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h3></div>

This topic examines quality management, different health care organizations within which the nurse manager functions and also the types of nursing care delivery systems. You should now be able to apply various concepts already learned, which will enable you to manage the nursing care services in your organizations more effectively and efficiently.</p>
